<p><b><a href="/wiki/October" title="October">October</a></b> <b><a href="/wiki/2003" title="2003">2003</a></b> was the tenth month of that common year. The month, which began on a <a href="/wiki/Wednesday" title="Wednesday">Wednesday</a>, ended on a <a href="/wiki/Friday" title="Friday">Friday</a> after 31 days.</p>
<p></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_1.2C_2003_.28Wednesday.29">October 1, 2003 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: October 1, 2003 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/President_of_South_Korea" title="President of South Korea">South Korean President</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roh_Moo_Hyun" title="Roh Moo Hyun">Roh Moo Hyun</a> reiterates offer to the United States to consider a request for South Korean participation in <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Force_%E2%80%93_Iraq" title="Multi-National Force – Iraq">Multi-National Force – Iraq</a> in exchange for "positive" movement to resolve the standoff over North Korea's <a href="/wiki/North_Korea_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="North Korea and weapons of mass destruction">nuclear weapons program</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-American_sentiment" title="Anti-American sentiment">Anti-Americanism</a>: A panel chosen by the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">administration of President George W. Bush</a> concludes that the United States must drastically increase and overhaul its <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> efforts to recast its image among Muslims and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arabs</a> abroad. "Hostility toward America has reached shocking levels ... What is required is not merely tactical adaptation but strategic, and radical, transformation."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a> unveils a proposal to boost flagging economic growth in Europe. The plan has two main parts: increasing spending on European transport networks and promoting research and development.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_a_Constitution_for_Europe" title="Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe">Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe</a>: Following talks with <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Prime Minister of the Czech Republic">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladim%C3%ADr_%C5%A0pidla" title="Vladimír Špidla">Vladimír Špidla</a> on the draft <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> constitution and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>'s position on the document, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="President of the Czech Republic">Czech President</a> <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Klaus" title="Václav Klaus">Václav Klaus</a> decides not to travel to Rome and attend the forthcoming intergovernmental conference.</li>
<li>Canada: <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Northwest_Territories" title="Premier of the Northwest Territories">Premier of the Northwest Territories</a> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Kakfwi" title="Stephen Kakfwi">Stephen Kakfwi</a> announces he will not seek re-election in the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories_general_election,_2003" title="Northwest Territories general election, 2003">November election</a>.</li>
<li>The website <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4chan.org" title="4chan.org">4chan.org</a> is created.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_2.2C_2003_.28Thursday.29">October 2, 2003 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: October 2, 2003 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> claims to "have already <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fuel_cycle" title="Nuclear fuel cycle">processed</a>" 8,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuel_rod" title="Fuel rod">fuel rods</a> from its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yongbyon_nuclear_reactor" title="Yongbyon nuclear reactor">Yongbyon nuclear reactor</a> north of <a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">Pyongyang</a> and is using the <a href="/wiki/Plutonium" title="Plutonium">plutonium</a> extracted during the process to make <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" title="Atomic bomb">atomic bombs</a> to boost its nuclear capabilities for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_deterrence" title="Nuclear deterrence">nuclear deterrent</a> force. Citing a "hostile policy" by the United States, Vice Foreign Minister <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Choe_Su_Hon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Choe Su Hon (page does not exist)">Choe Su Hon</a> states this is a means to safeguard the country's territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> discusses a new United States draft resolution on <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, which would enhance the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>' role in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary General of the United Nations">Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> states draft did not go in the direction he recommended. A quicker transfer of <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> "<i>may change the dynamics on the ground, in terms of the security situation, and send a message</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">Technology</a> – <a href="/wiki/Genome" title="Genome">Genome</a>: The genome chip arrived with several companies rushing to sell the known human genes. The products will allow scientists to scan all genes in a human tissue sample at once to determine which are active, with lower cost and increased speed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-American_relations" title="Sino-American relations">Sino-American relations</a>: The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> blames China for the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Island_incident" title="Hainan Island incident">Hainan Island incident</a>. A report released to <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jane%27s_Defense_Weekly" title="Jane's Defense Weekly">Jane's Defense Weekly</a></i> under the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Information_Act_(United_States)" title="Freedom of Information Act (United States)">Freedom of Information Act</a> said that the pilot of the Chinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jet_fighter" title="Jet fighter">jet fighter</a> made three passes at the U.S. propeller-driven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconnaissance_plane" title="Reconnaissance plane">reconnaissance plane</a> over <a href="/wiki/International_waters" title="International waters">international waters</a>. On the third pass, the Chinese fighter hit a propeller on the American plane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ontario_general_election,_2003" title="Ontario general election, 2003">Ontario general election, 2003</a>: <a href="/wiki/Dalton_McGuinty" title="Dalton McGuinty">Dalton McGuinty</a> becomes the new premier of <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> when his party defeats <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Eves" title="Ernie Eves">Ernie Eves</a>'s incumbent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ontario_Progressive_Conservative_Party" title="Ontario Progressive Conservative Party">Tories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hampton" title="Howard Hampton">Howard Hampton</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ontario_New_Democratic_Party" title="Ontario New Democratic Party">NDP</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J._M._Coetzee" title="J. M. Coetzee">J. M. Coetzee</a> wins <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_literature" title="Nobel Prize for literature">Nobel Prize for literature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>: United States draft legislation which urges <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">The Pentagon</a> to buy defence parts from American manufacturers has turned heads in Brussels, with some warning of yet another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_dispute" title="Trade dispute">trade dispute</a> at the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>: The first bilateral meeting between France and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> since 1998 is marked by disagreements over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Constitution" title="European Constitution">European Constitution</a>. Austria heads the group of small countries seeking to make changes to the text, but France wants to leave the draft by <a href="/wiki/Val%C3%A9ry_Giscard_d%27Estaing" title="Valéry Giscard d'Estaing">Valéry Giscard d'Estaing</a> broadly untouched.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">Media</a>: A <a href="/wiki/Program_on_International_Policy_Attitudes" title="Program on International Policy Attitudes">Program on International Policy Attitudes</a> (PIPA) study conducted with <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>-based Knowledge Networks, titled "Misperceptions, the Media, and the Iraq War," is released. According to this study, misperceptions about the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a> are most common among consumers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News Channel</a> and supporters of President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and least common among consumers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">PBS</a> and <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> and supporters of Democratic presidential candidates. The study also found that frequent viewers of Fox News are more likely to believe in the misconceptions than less frequent ones. One example misconception is the belief that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a> have already been found in Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_3.2C_2003_.28Friday.29">October 3, 2003 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: October 3, 2003 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-Earth_asteroid" title="Near-Earth asteroid">Near-Earth asteroid</a>: Confirmation on the closest near-miss of a natural object ever recorded. The asteroid (designated <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=2003_SQ222&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="2003 SQ222 (page does not exist)">2003 SQ222</a>), about the size of a small house, flew past Earth at a distance of around 88,000 kilometres. It would have made a fireball had it entered the atmosphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iraq_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Iraq and weapons of mass destruction">Iraq and weapons of mass destruction</a>: The world continues to digest David Kay's report that finds very little evidence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Weapons of mass destruction">Weapons of mass destruction</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, although the regime did intend to develop more weapons with additional capabilities. Such plans and programs appear to have been dormant, the existence of these were also concealed from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> during the inspections that began in 2002. Weapons inspectors in Iraq do find clandestine "<i>network of biological <a href="/wiki/Laboratory" title="Laboratory">laboratories</a></i>" and a deadly strain of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Botulinum" title="Botulinum">botulinum</a>. The US-sponsored search for WMD has so far cost <span class="nowrap">$300 million</span> and is projected to cost around <span class="nowrap">$600 million</span> more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_California_recall" title="2003 California recall">California recall</a>: <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> denies admiring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitler" title="Hitler">Hitler</a>. Arnold Schwarzenegger's denial comes days before the vote for the next <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a> of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wesley_Clark" title="Wesley Clark">General Wesley Clark</a> suggests that members of the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush</a> administration may be liable to criminal charges in connection with the <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> war. Clark alleges that the plans for the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>, and other interventions in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> (possibly including <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>), pre-dated the inauguration of the President and that the reasons for the war were misleadingly presented to the US people.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> said that <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Lozada" title="Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada">Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, may be preparing a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> (in Spanish)</li>
<li>Polish soldiers of the United States-led Coalition discovered four advanced <a href="/wiki/Missile" title="Missile">missiles</a> around central <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> in the Hilla region near a highway. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roland_missile" title="Roland missile">Roland-type</a> French-made missiles (which are fired from a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_launcher_vehicle" title="Mobile launcher vehicle">mobile launcher vehicle</a> against low flying aircraft) were initially believed to have been manufactured earlier in 2003. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Arms_export&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Arms export (page does not exist)">Arms exports</a> to Iraq had been barred by the United Nations after the 1990 invasion of <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>. France says it last shipped Roland missiles to Iraq in 1986. The Polish soldiers were later found to have misinterpreted markings that read 07-01-KND 2003 as a date on the missiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters2_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters2-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_4.2C_2003_.28Saturday.29">October 4, 2003 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: October 4, 2003 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_bomber" title="Suicide bomber">suicide bomber</a> blows herself up in a crowded beach restaurant in the northern <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> port city of <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>, killing at least 19 people and wounding about two dozen, at least six seriously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Hours later Israeli helicopter gunships retaliate by attacking targets in Gaza City and Central Gaza.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robin_Cook" title="Robin Cook">Robin Cook</a>, former United Kingdom <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Affairs" title="Secretary of State for Foreign and Commonwealth Affairs">Foreign Secretary</a> who resigned from the British Government in protest prior the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_occupation_of_Iraq_timeline" title="2003 occupation of Iraq timeline">Iraq war</a>, publishes his personal diaries. In them he alleges <i>inter alia</i> that <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> knew before the Iraq war began that the <a href="/wiki/September_Dossier" title="September Dossier">45 minutes to launch claim</a> was false.</li>
<li>Poland apologizes to France for its claims that it had found newly produced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roland_missile" title="Roland missile">Roland</a> <a href="/wiki/Surface-to-air_missile" title="Surface-to-air missile">surface-to-air missiles</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. It is believed that the Polish soldiers misinterpreted a "use-by" date or installation date marked on the missiles as a date of production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters2_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters2-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_5.2C_2003_.28Sunday.29">October 5, 2003 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: October 5, 2003 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maher_Arar" title="Maher Arar">Maher Arar</a> is reported to have been freed from a <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syrian</a> jail. The Canadian engineer was deported to Syria by the United States as he changed planes in New York, over a year ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> He will arrive in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> the following afternoon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ain_es_Saheb_airstrike" title="Ain es Saheb airstrike">Ain es Saheb airstrike</a>: <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> warplanes attack an alleged <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Jihad_Movement_in_Palestine" title="Islamic Jihad Movement in Palestine">Islamic Jihad</a> training base deep in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> in retaliation for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_bombing" title="Suicide bombing">suicide bombing</a> at a Haifa restaurant that killed 19 people, the army said Sunday. Israeli media state this is the first Israeli attack on Syrian soil in more than two decades. An emergency session of the UN Security Council is scheduled to debate the action. France and Germany condemn the attack. The international community calls for restraint by all parties involved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> canonizes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daniele_Comboni" title="Daniele Comboni">Daniele Comboni</a> (1831–1881), <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Janssen" title="Arnold Janssen">Arnold Janssen</a> (1837–1909) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josef_Freinademetz" title="Josef Freinademetz">Josef Freinademetz</a> (1852–1908).</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ireland_on_Sunday" title="Ireland on Sunday">Ireland on Sunday</a></i> claims that <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> is suffering from terminal <a href="/wiki/Stomach_cancer" title="Stomach cancer">stomach cancer</a> which has spread to his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colon_(anatomy)" title="Colon (anatomy)">colon</a>. The newspaper reports that the Pope has dictated a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Living_will" title="Living will">living will</a> which gives instructions as to how the Roman Catholic Church is to be administered when the medical treatment he is receiving makes it impossible for him to function as pope. According to the paper, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">Cardinals</a> have been told to be ready at a moment's notice to fly to <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> for a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Papal_funeral&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Papal funeral (page does not exist)">Papal funeral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave" title="Papal conclave">Papal conclave</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_6.2C_2003_.28Monday.29">October 6, 2003 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: October 6, 2003 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Democratic_Party_Presidential_Primary,_2004" title="U.S. Democratic Party Presidential Primary, 2004">2004 U.S. Democratic Primaries</a>: Senator <a href="/wiki/Bob_Graham" title="Bob Graham">Bob Graham</a> announces on <i><a href="/wiki/Larry_King_Live" title="Larry King Live">Larry King Live</a></i> that he is ending his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004">2004 presidential</a> campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chechen_Election&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chechen Election (page does not exist)">Chechen Election</a>: <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>'s choice, the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Kremlin" title="Moscow Kremlin">Kremlin</a>-backed <a href="/wiki/Akhmad_Kadyrov" title="Akhmad Kadyrov">Akhmad Kadyrov</a> swept presidential election in the Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Chechnya" title="Republic of Chechnya">republic of Chechnya</a>, winning 81 percent of the votes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SCO_v._IBM_Linux_lawsuit" title="SCO v. IBM Linux lawsuit">SCO v. IBM</a>: In an open letter to the <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> community published by <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">Silicon Graphics</a> (SGI), SGI states it conducted a comprehensive comparison of the <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux kernel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UNIX_System_V" title="UNIX System V">UNIX System V</a> <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> owned by The <a href="/wiki/SCO_Group" title="SCO Group">SCO Group</a>. According to the letter (authored by SGI <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vice_President" title="Vice President">Vice President</a> of <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">Software</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rich_Altmaier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rich Altmaier (page does not exist)">Rich Altmaier</a>), SGI's "<i>exhaustive comparison</i>" of the source codes turned up only "<i>trivial</i>" code segments that "<i>may arguably be related</i>" to SCO's software. The letter also disputed SCO's claims that SGI inappropriately contributed its <a href="/wiki/XFS" title="XFS">XFS</a> (eXtensible File System).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>: Facing renewed threats from <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, Palestinian leader <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, declares a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> in Palestinian areas and installs a new <a href="/wiki/Forms_of_government" title="Forms of government">government</a> by decree. <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Qurei" title="Ahmed Qurei">Ahmed Qurei</a> is appointed <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> and head of the eight-member emergency cabinet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>: In his first public comments since the Israeli attack on Syria, President Bush says that Israel has the right to defend its homeland; at the same time Mr. Bush asks Prime Minister Sharon to avoid any further actions that might destabilize the region.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Lauterbur" title="Paul Lauterbur">Paul Lauterbur</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Peter_Mansfield" title="Peter Mansfield">Peter Mansfield</a> are jointly awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a> for their discoveries concerning <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnetic_Resonance_Imaging" title="Magnetic Resonance Imaging">Magnetic Resonance Imaging</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: Some in the international community have rejected a revised United States draft <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolution" title="United Nations Security Council resolution">United Nations Security Council resolution</a> concerning <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> (calling for a multinational force of peacekeeping troops in Iraq under American command; transferring power gradually to elected civilian rule [though there is no handover timetable for sovereignty]). The resolution is being supported by the United Kingdom. France, Germany, and Russia (which opposed the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>) have joined <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> in opposing the resolution. Annan states that the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> itself will not become heavily involved unless there are early moves toward passing sovereignty to the Iraqi people. Annan's stance is similar to that of <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> and some members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>Attempts by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>'s government to ban smoking in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_house" title="Public house">pubs</a>, restaurants and hotels run into more trouble as a government minister who will have responsibility for enforcing the ban, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Fahey" title="Frank Fahey">Frank Fahey</a>, refuses to deny that he is critical of the plan and wants a compromise that would allow smoking in some areas to continue. A former <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Galway" title="Mayor of Galway">Mayor of Galway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fianna_F%C3%A1il" title="Fianna Fáil">Fianna Fáil</a> councillor who has links with the pub industry resigns from a health authority in protest at the refusal of the Fianna Fáil-<a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democrats" title="Progressive Democrats">Progressive Democrat</a> government to compromise on the proposed ban. This follows an earlier announcement that publicans in <a href="/wiki/County_Kerry" title="County Kerry">County Kerry</a> will refuse to obey the new law and indications of growing popular opposition to the ban.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>Former <a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a> correspondent <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=James_Furlong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="James Furlong (page does not exist)">James Furlong</a>, who resigned over allegations that he had faked a report during the Iraq War, is found dead. Furlong, aged 44, had served as Sky News' Defence and Royal Correspondent. He had previously worked for <a href="/wiki/ITN" title="ITN">ITN</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> report says that almost <span class="nowrap">1 billion</span> people worldwide are living in <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a>. By 2050 <span class="nowrap">3 billion</span>, out of a world urban population of <span class="nowrap">6 billion</span>, may be living in slums, unless radical policies are implemented, according to the UN. Dr Anna Tibaijuka of the UN says the persistence of the slums should shame the whole world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_7.2C_2003_.28Tuesday.29">October 7, 2003 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: October 7, 2003 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_California_recall" title="2003 California recall">California recall</a>: The state of California held a special election to decide whether to recall <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Gray_Davis" title="Gray Davis">Gray Davis</a>, and, if so, who to replace him with. Also on the ballot: <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_53_(2003)" title="California Proposition 53 (2003)">Proposition 53</a>, the "California Twenty-First Century Infrastructure Investment Fund," and <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_54_(2003)" title="California Proposition 54 (2003)">Proposition 54</a>, the "Racial Privacy Initiative."</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Nobel Prize in Physics</a> is awarded jointly to <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Alexeyevich_Abrikosov" title="Alexei Alexeyevich Abrikosov">Alexei Abrikosov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitaly_Ginzburg" title="Vitaly Ginzburg">Vitaly Ginzburg</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthony_Leggett" title="Anthony Leggett">Anthony Leggett</a> for their work on the theory of <a href="/wiki/Superconductivity" title="Superconductivity">superconductors</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superfluid" title="Superfluid">superfluids</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> envoy and Special Coordinator for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_East_peace_process" title="Middle East peace process">Middle East peace process</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terje_Roed-Larsen" title="Terje Roed-Larsen">Terje Roed-Larsen</a>, condemns attack from <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanese_territory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lebanese territory (page does not exist)">Lebanese territory</a> that killed an <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> soldier across the southern withdrawal line and urges <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> to control the use of force everywhere in its jurisdiction. Roed-Larsen, states the attack "constitutes a clear violation of the Blue Line and Security Council resolutions and could escalate tension between Israel and its northern neighbours" and he calls on all sides to use <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a> and take no action that "could increase the already high level of tension in the region".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>UN spokesman states that a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peacekeeping_operation" title="Peacekeeping operation">peacekeeping operation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (DRC) has discovered 65 bodies, mostly children, apparently massacred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Turkey" title="Parliament of Turkey">Turkish Parliament</a> votes (358-to-183) to approve the dispatch of <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeepers</a> to <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, in a major victory for United States efforts to broaden foreign involvement in Iraq. In <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Governing_Council" title="Iraqi Governing Council">Iraqi Governing Council</a> officials state that they would oppose any new foreign troop deployment to Iraq. No formal decision had been made by the Council and leaders of the council have stated they would support this if the United States requested this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> government announce they would not prosecute the five policemen accused of killing <a href="/wiki/Steve_Biko" title="Steve Biko">Steve Biko</a> in 1977, citing insufficient evidence to support a murder charge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN) announces its intention to form a single-market "Asian Community" by 2020.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_8.2C_2003_.28Wednesday.29">October 8, 2003 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: October 8, 2003 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a> is awarded jointly to <a href="/wiki/Peter_Agre" title="Peter Agre">Peter Agre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roderick_MacKinnon" title="Roderick MacKinnon">Roderick MacKinnon</a> for discoveries concerning <a href="/wiki/Aquaporin" title="Aquaporin">aquaporins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ion_channel" title="Ion channel">ion channels</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cell_membrane" title="Cell membrane">cell membranes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_California_recall" title="2003 California recall">California recall</a>: <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> wins the election with 48.6% after voters decide to recall <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">California Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Gray_Davis" title="Gray Davis">Gray Davis</a>. Schwarzenegger's closest rival was the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_California" title="Lieutenant Governor of California">Lieutenant Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Cruz_Bustamante" title="Cruz Bustamante">Cruz Bustamante</a>, with 31.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI">FBI</a> admits that hidden listening devices planted in the office of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Philadelphia" title="Mayor of Philadelphia">Mayor of Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, were placed there by FBI agents. It is currently not known if the Mayor of Philadelphia is a target of an investigation nor is there any details provided about the nature of the probe that the device was part of. A <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">law enforcement</a> official cautions that the presence of the listening devices does not necessarily mean that the mayor, himself, is under investigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> has suffered a mild <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">heart attack</a>. Palestinian leadership officials tried to hide condition of the <a href="/wiki/President" title="President">president</a>. "Although he has had a slight heart attack, the doctors say he will make a full recovery. He is in full control. There is nothing to worry about," states close aide to Arafat. Officials state that it would "have created <a href="/wiki/Panic" title="Panic">panic</a> at a critical time when the <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israelis</a> are threatening Arafat's life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_9.2C_2003_.28Thursday.29">October 9, 2003 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: October 9, 2003 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i>Time</i> magazine reports that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yassir_Arafat" title="Yassir Arafat">Yassir Arafat</a>, whose health has led to confused reporting over the past days, with him variously reported as having had flu and having had a heart attack, in actuality has <a href="/wiki/Stomach_cancer" title="Stomach cancer">stomach cancer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> successfully <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Test_fire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Test fire (page does not exist)">test fires</a> a medium-range, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear</a>-capable <a href="/wiki/Missile" title="Missile">missile</a>, the second such <a href="/wiki/Quality_control" title="Quality control">test</a> in less than a <a href="/wiki/Week" title="Week">week</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistan_army" title="Pakistan army">Pakistan army</a> states. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hatf-4_missile&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hatf-4 missile (page does not exist)">Hatf-4 missile</a>, also known as the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shaheen_1_missile&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shaheen 1 missile (page does not exist)">Shaheen 1</a>, was fired off, according to the <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">army</a>. The missile has a range of 435 miles, meaning it can hit most major targets in India. The test followed a similar launching on Friday of the short-range <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hatf-2_Ghaznavi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hatf-2 Ghaznavi (page does not exist)">Hatf-2 Ghaznavi</a> after which Pakistan said it was in the middle of a series of such tests. Pakistani army <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spokesman" title="Spokesman">spokesman</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_General" title="Major General">Major General</a> <a href="/wiki/Shaukat_Sultan" title="Shaukat Sultan">Shaukat Sultan</a> said India had been told of each of the launches beforehand and he states the tests should not affect the <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> between the two neighbors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Shaul_Mofaz" title="Shaul Mofaz">Shaul Mofaz</a> ordered dispatches of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> <a href="/wiki/Troop" title="Troop">troop</a> reinforcements to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Palestinian_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Palestinian Area (page does not exist)">Palestinian Areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>, and weighed a call-up of reserves, citing new warnings about planned attacks by Palestinian militants. The Israeli military also extended a two-<a href="/wiki/Week" title="Week">week</a> <a href="/wiki/Embargo" title="Embargo">lockdown</a> on Palestinians' travel within the West Bank and Gaza in what it states as a bid to prevent further attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Meanwhile, prime minister Ahmed Qurei is reported to have declined to form a government and told President Yasser Arafat he wants to quit his post.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: Twin attacks in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> killed a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Diplomat" title="Diplomat">diplomat</a> (by gunshot) and, in the other, at least ten people following an attack on a <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">police</a> station in Baghdad's main <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shi%27ite" title="Shi'ite">Shi'ite</a> neighbourhood, exactly half a year since <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Coalition_troop&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Coalition troop (page does not exist)">Coalition troops</a> occupied the Iraqi city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_10.2C_2003_.28Friday.29">October 10, 2003 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: October 10, 2003 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shirin_Ebadi" title="Shirin Ebadi">Shirin Ebadi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a> human rights lawyer, is awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> two more soldiers are killed and four wounded in an ambush in the Sadr district of Baghdad. The troops are lured into the ambush by civilians in what could be a new tactic by hostile forces in Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camp_X-ray" title="Camp X-ray">Camp X-ray</a>: The United States' policy of detaining up to 600 people in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detainment_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detainment camp">Guantanamo Bay</a> comes under fierce attack from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> and a group of American former judges, diplomats and military officers who are asking the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> to review the situation. The Red Cross criticises the policy of holding detainees without legal representation and in contravention of legal conventions; it reports a worrying deterioration in the mental health of detainees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> military officer states Palestinian militants are feared to be using a tunnel to smuggle <a href="/wiki/Anti-tank_missile" title="Anti-tank missile">anti-tank missiles</a> and portable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-aircraft_missile" title="Anti-aircraft missile">anti-aircraft missiles</a>, though no tunnels had been found yet. The <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">army</a> states it is encountering strong resistance from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinians</a> using dozens of homemade <a href="/wiki/Bomb" title="Bomb">bombs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocket-propelled_grenade" title="Rocket-propelled grenade">rocket-propelled grenades</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Grenade" title="Grenade">grenades</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machine_gun" title="Machine gun">automatic weapons</a>. One <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> child and four adults killed in overnight attack on <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a> refugee camp in <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a>: The <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003 Rugby World Cup</a>, with 20 countries competing for the <a href="/wiki/William_Webb_Ellis" title="William Webb Ellis">William Webb Ellis</a> Trophy over a seven-week period, starts after a spectacular opening ceremony at the Telstra Stadium, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, Australia, with Australia defeating <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> 24–8 in the opening match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Johan-Friso_of_the_Netherlands" title="Prince Johan-Friso of the Netherlands">Prince Johan-Friso of the Netherlands</a>, second son of Queen Beatrix and second in line of succession to the throne will lose his succession rights when he marries Mabel Wisse Smit without the Dutch Parliament's permission. Government assent was refused because the couple had been less than candid about the bride's interactions with gangster Klaas Bruisma in the late 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_11.2C_2003_.28Saturday.29">October 11, 2003 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: October 11, 2003 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: Israeli troops pull back in <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza</a>. Israel will continue to demolish tunnels. The Israeli army states it discovers three tunnels in the camp, but no weapons have been found. A Palestinian teenager is shot dead and up to 10 homes were demolished and [ater and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Electricity_facility&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Electricity facility (page does not exist)">electricity facilities</a> were hit. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> militants were seeking to smuggle from <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> shoulder-fired missiles that could be used against tanks, helicopters, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fighter_jet" title="Fighter jet">fighter jets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> proposes a change in <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service" title="United States Fish and Wildlife Service">United States Fish and Wildlife Service</a> regulations which would allow American citizens to travel abroad to capture, kill, and import <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered species</a>. The regulation would not allow Americans to do the same to endangered species inside the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li>German magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> reports that <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> is preparing an attack on <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a> atomic plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> says that it will retaliate if attacked by Israel again. A week after Israel's attack the two countries continue to exchange insults; the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> is unable to agree on a resolution condemning Israel's attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Conference</a> (OIC), a grouping of Muslim nations meeting in Malaysia, calls on the US to quit Iraq as soon as possible and to hand over to the UN; the OIC also pledges support to Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Japan" title="House of Representatives of Japan">House of Representatives</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diet_of_Japan" title="Diet of Japan">Diet of Japan</a> is dissolved by the Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koizumi_Junichiro" title="Koizumi Junichiro">Koizumi Junichiro</a> and the election will take place on November 9, 2003. See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_general_election,_2003" title="Japan general election, 2003">Japan general election, 2003</a> for more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Spanish rail company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RENFE" title="RENFE">RENFE</a> opens its second <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> high-speed line, serving <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guadalajara,_Spain" title="Guadalajara, Spain">Guadalajara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calatayud" title="Calatayud">Calatayud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">Zaragoza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lleida" title="Lleida">Lleida</a>. It is expected to reach <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> by 2005. (Another line is being built from Madrid to <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, and others to <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> are planned.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_12.2C_2003_.28Sunday.29">October 12, 2003 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: October 12, 2003 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a>: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> prevents India from snatching victory in the first <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test cricket</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ahmedabad" title="Ahmedabad">Ahmedabad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li>Relations between Syria and the United States fall to a low point as Syria criticizes the US for its failure to censure Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li>China confirms that it will launch its first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manned_space_mission" title="Manned space mission">manned space mission</a> between October 15 and 17. The <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a> plans to <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbit</a> Earth 14 times before landing in an undisclosed location. (See <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_5" title="Shenzhou 5">Shenzhou 5</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li>The operation to separate two-year-old <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> twins joined at the head is going well in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas</a>; the two boys have been separated and no troublesome complications have arisen. The next steps are to reconstruct the boys' skulls including the skin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>India, Thailand, and China press ahead with efforts and a study group aimed at creating a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Area" title="Free Trade Area">Free Trade Area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-invasion_Iraq,_2003%E2%80%93present" title="Post-invasion Iraq, 2003–present">2003 occupation of Iraq</a>: A huge explosion occurs in the center of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, possibly caused by car bomb. A number of fatalities are reported. The blast takes place in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad_Hotel" title="Baghdad Hotel">Baghdad Hotel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
<li>[Researchers announced that they have discovered the detailed relationship between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ras_v12" title="Ras v12">Ras v12</a> gene, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Polarity_gene&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Polarity gene (page does not exist)">polarity genes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Metastasis" title="Metastasis">metastasis</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a> in <a href="/wiki/Drosophila_melanogaster" title="Drosophila melanogaster">fruit flies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li>Liberia drops diplomatic relations with the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and re-establishes ties with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. This move was seen largely as a result of China's lobbying in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, which is planning to deploy a peacekeeping force to Liberia. Taiwanese Foreign Minister Eugene Chien offers to resign as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_13.2C_2003_.28Monday.29">October 13, 2003 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: October 13, 2003 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-invasion_Iraq,_2003%E2%80%93present" title="Post-invasion Iraq, 2003–present">2003 occupation of Iraq</a>: New draft resolution being circulated at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> aims at getting international aid. The resolution sets a deadline for initial steps, if only for a transitional step, toward restoring <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a>, giving the <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Governing_Council" title="Iraqi Governing Council">Iraqi Governing Council</a> until December 15 to develop a timetable for writing a <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a> and holding <a href="/wiki/Election" title="Election">elections</a>. The <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush administration</a> proposes that the United Nations recognize the Iraqi Governing Council as a unit that "will embody the sovereignty" of Iraq until the country returns to self-rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> incursion leaves 1,240 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinians</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homeless" title="Homeless">homeless</a>, UN agency finds. The Israeli demolition of <a href="/wiki/Refugee_shelter" title="Refugee shelter">refugee shelters</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a> camp on the southern <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a> last week has left 1,240 people homeless, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> relief workers state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bertie_Ahern" title="Bertie Ahern">Bertie Ahern</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, have begun talks in <a href="/wiki/10_Downing_Street" title="10 Downing Street">Downing Street</a> on a possible restoration of devolved government in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-invasion_Iraq,_2003%E2%80%93present" title="Post-invasion Iraq, 2003–present">2003 occupation of Iraq</a>: Three more US soldiers have been killed in separate incidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Library_of_Science" title="Public Library of Science">Public Library of Science</a> commences publication of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_access_(publishing)" title="Open access (publishing)">open-access</a> <a href="/wiki/Scientific_journal" title="Scientific journal">scientific journal</a>, <i>PLoS Biology</i> and its website is immediately overwhelmed by traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_14.2C_2003_.28Tuesday.29">October 14, 2003 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: October 14, 2003 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidió Teilifís Éireann">RTÉ</a>'s <i>Prime Time</i> current affairs programme reports that <a href="/wiki/Cahal_Daly" title="Cahal Daly">Cahal Daly</a>, Bishop of Down and Conor, refused to accept allegations passed on to him by students of improper sexual conduct by Monsignor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Micheal_Ledwith" title="Micheal Ledwith">Micheal Ledwith</a>, then head of <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_College,_Maynooth" title="St Patrick's College, Maynooth">St Patrick's College, Maynooth</a>, Ireland's major <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a>. According to the programme Daly became aggressive, telling students "go back and say your prayers". The TV programme confirms that Daly, and his predecessor, Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_%C3%93_Fiaich" title="Tomás Ó Fiaich">Tomás Ó Fiaich</a>, were centrally involved in efforts to silence critics of Ledwith, including forcing the resignation of one dean of students who informed them of allegations that Ledwith was making sexual advances against student priests. Ledwith subsequently left the college after paying damages to an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Under-age" title="Under-age">under-age</a> teenager to whom he allegedly made sexual advances. Ledwith, once an internationally famous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theologian</a> tipped to become Catholic <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Dublin_(Roman_Catholic)" title="Archbishop of Dublin (Roman Catholic)">Archbishop of Dublin</a>, is now associated with an American <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a> organization. Having been tracked down by the programme, Ledwith refuses to comment 'for legal reasons'.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>: The Inauguration of a new government takes place. The rebels are expected to disarm.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sniper" title="Sniper">Sniper</a> – <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">Terrorism</a>: Trial of <a href="/wiki/John_Allen_Muhammad" title="John Allen Muhammad">John Allen Muhammad</a>, who is suspected of being the Washington DC serial sniper, begins. He pleads not guilty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> reports that dissident <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army" title="Irish Republican Army">IRA</a> groups are supplying the weapons that have led to a recent surge in UK gun crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chatrooms" title="Chatrooms">chatrooms</a> close today. Free unmoderated chatrooms outside the US are closed in what Microsoft claim is an attempt to safeguard children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: Israel orders the expulsion of 15 Palestinian detainees from the West Bank to the Gaza Strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li>British <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a> leader, <a href="/wiki/Iain_Duncan_Smith" title="Iain Duncan Smith">Iain Duncan Smith</a>, is being investigated by Parliamentary Standards Commissioner Sir <a href="/wiki/Philip_Mawer" title="Philip Mawer">Philip Mawer</a> over allegations that he paid a secretarial salary to his wife without her doing sufficient work to warrant the payments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
<li>A British <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> carrier is found guilty of causing grievous bodily harm after infecting two lovers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_15.2C_2003_.28Wednesday.29">October 15, 2003 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: October 15, 2003 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-invasion_Iraq,_2003%E2%80%93present" title="Post-invasion Iraq, 2003–present">2003 occupation of Iraq</a>: U.S. concessions to proposals from Russia, the China and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> ensure their support for a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> resolution to provide greater international legitimacy to the occupation force and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraq_Interim_Governing_Council" title="Iraq Interim Governing Council">Iraq Interim Governing Council</a>. The resolution draft, legitimizing US military and political control over Iraq's political future, was already supported by <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>. Russia agrees to act as a mediator to achieve support for the compromise also from Germany and France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: Four people die in a bomb attack on a convoy of US diplomatic vehicles in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>. Palestinian Authority head <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> calls the bombing "dirty and shameful" in an exclusive interview on <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC News</a>. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">Colin Powell</a> urges <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Prime Minister of the Palestinian National Authority">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Qurei" title="Ahmed Qurei">Ahmed Qurei</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">telephone</a> call "<i>to take action to put an end to violence and terrorism</i>," according to a Palestinian official.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li>China launches its first <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronaut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yang_Liwei" title="Yang Liwei">Yang Liwei</a> into orbit aboard a <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_(spacecraft)" title="Shenzhou (spacecraft)">Shenzhou</a> spacecraft, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_5" title="Shenzhou 5">Shenzhou 5</a>. The 21-hour trip is planned to circle the planet 14 times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-invasion_Iraq,_2003%E2%80%93present" title="Post-invasion Iraq, 2003–present">2003 occupation of Iraq</a>: Japan offers <span class="nowrap">$1.5 billion</span> aid to Iraq in what could be the first tranche of a total of <span class="nowrap">$5 billion</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> <a href="/wiki/Certiorari" title="Certiorari">agreed to hear</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Elk_Grove_Unified_School_District_v._Newdow" title="Elk Grove Unified School District v. Newdow">Elk Grove Unified School District v. Newdow</a></i></li>
<li>The Irish-based Australian novelist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D.B.C._Pierre" title="D.B.C. Pierre">D.B.C. Pierre</a> (real name Peter Finlay) wins the 2003 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Booker_prize" title="Booker prize">Booker prize</a> with his first novel, <a href="/wiki/Vernon_God_Little" title="Vernon God Little">Vernon God Little</a>, a satire on a Texas high-school massacre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> leaders from around the world meet in <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_Palace" title="Lambeth Palace">Lambeth Palace</a> in an attempt to avoid a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schism_(religion)" title="Schism (religion)">schism</a> on the issue of <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> in the clergy. The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Ireland" title="Church of Ireland">Church of Ireland</a> <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Armagh_(Church_of_Ireland)" title="Archbishop of Armagh (Church of Ireland)">Archbishop of Armagh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Eames" title="Robin Eames">Robin Eames</a> says that the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a> is moving towards a "consensus situation" on the issue of <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> and the clergy at its meeting in <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_Palace" title="Lambeth Palace">Lambeth Palace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-94">[94]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: The United States <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">vetoes</a> a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> resolution condemning the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier" title="Israeli West Bank barrier">Israeli West Bank barrier</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Alliance" title="Canadian Alliance">Canadian Alliance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Progressive Conservative Party of Canada">Progressive Conservative Party of Canada</a> strike a deal to merge. The deal creating the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Conservative Party of Canada">Conservative Party of Canada</a> must be ratified by each party's membership before December 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>: Presidential elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Steven Gerrard becomes captain of Liverpool Football Club.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_16.2C_2003_.28Thursday.29">October 16, 2003 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: October 16, 2003 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> unanimously approves a new US resolution on <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. Russia, Germany and France back the resolution but will not provide troops or money.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> A survey indicates poor morale amongst the US troops serving in Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li>President Bush re-affirms his intention to pressure China and Japan into fair policies re their exchange rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> China's trade surplus is shrinking as imports surge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> At the same time India is wrestling with the implications of the sustained appreciation of the rupee against the dollar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></li>
<li>Tens of thousands of Catholics attend <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a> celebrating the 25th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> in Rome. The Pope will beatify <a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a> on Sunday, October 19, and install 30 new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">Cardinals</a> on Tuesday, October 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></li>
<li>In a surprise move, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monsanto_Company" title="Monsanto Company">Monsanto Company</a> announce their intention to quit the European cereal business. Citing lack of success, the company has decided to cut costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: European Commissioner for External Relations, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Patten" title="Chris Patten">Chris Patten</a> has questioned <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>'s commitment to a two-states resolution to the conflict with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_(identity)" title="Palestinian (identity)">Palestinians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
<li>China's first astronaut, <a href="/wiki/Yang_Liwei" title="Yang Liwei">Yang Liwei</a> returns to earth safely aboard a Shenzhou spacecraft, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhou_5" title="Shenzhou 5">Shenzhou 5</a>. During the 21-hour trip, he circled the planet 14 times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apple_Computer" title="Apple Computer">Apple</a> launches its iTunes Music Store, an online download music store, for the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> platform. The iTunes software can be downloaded from <a class="external text" href="http://www.apple.com/" rel="nofollow">apple.com</a> for free.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="October_17.2C_2003_.28Friday.29">October 17, 2003 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/October_2003&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: October 17, 2003 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mesa" title="Carlos Mesa">Carlos Mesa</a> is sworn in as the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bolivia" title="President of Bolivia">President of Bolivia</a>, after former president <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Lozada" title="Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada">Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada</a> was forced to resign as protests and strikes escalated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivian_Gas_War" title="Bolivian Gas War">Bolivian Gas War</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_occupation_of_Iraq" title="American occupation of Iraq">Occupation of Iraq</a>: Four US troops and at least two police officers are killed in an ambush in <a href="/wiki/Karbala" title="Karbala">Karbala</a> and another incident in Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></li>
